We had left the Acari the evening prior and boated up to the confluence of the Rio Sucundari and Rio Campinarana. We all got in the boats at first light and made our away about 5 km to a large campinarana that rested right on the edge of the lake-like Rio Campaninara. Our party parked the boat at the downstream end and the other continued farther up so we weren't shooting at eachother. After Mike shot some, I took the gun for the remainder of the morning. The habitat was open white-sand grassland with low trees. A terra firme bluff overlooked the campinarana and a small inlet (igarape)  bordered the campinarana's eastern side. Finally, birds were easy to see and ID and it was a completely new avifauna for me. Lots of austral migrants as well. One of the best mornings of the trip!

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS201971692	2018-09-01 20:39:35	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			X				Brazil	BR	Mato Grosso	BR-MT							Serra dos Caiabis / Salto Apiacás	L2239268	P	-10.3420245	-56.9495201	2009-05-20	05:00:00	obsr412230	S14459406	Traveling	P22	EBIRD_CAN	420	17.000		2	1		0	1	0		The Serra dos Caiabis is a range of hills in central-north Mato Grosso which separate the Arinos and Teles Pires drainages in the southern Brazilian Amazon. This geomorphological formation is an accessible area to explore the Mato Grosso tropical dry forest, an ecotone habitat between the cerrado of central Brazil and the Amazon moist forests to the north and west. The biodiversity here is similar to that of the better-known Serra do Cachimbo in southern Pará, perhaps somewhat poorer but with the advantage of being relatively accessible in a day-trip from Alta Floresta, the primary regional centre. The Serra dos Caiabis is still poorly-known ornithologically, having been the subject of just one survey in 2005-06 (Lees et al. 2008) and a follow-up visit we made in June 2008. All previous birding visits to the Serra dos Caiabis had been to the area south-west of Garimpo do Cabeça along the semi-abandoned MT-325 roughly 70-100 km from Alta Floresta.----From Alta Floresta take the MT-208 west towards Nova Bandeirantes. 12 km from Alta Floresta bear left at an obvious fork in the road where the pavement ends. It begins again 100m on, and at present the road is surfaced as far as the Rio Santa Helena. At 89 km from Alta Floresta, you will see the Fazenda Apiacas on your right and an obvious dirt road heading off to the left with a large sign for Fazenda Bacaeri. Take this road (the MT-160) 55 km south and you will reach a fork signed to Juara on the left and the hydroelectric project at Salto Apiacas on the right. Taking the left fork the road soon begins to ascend the Serra dos Caiabis. There is good habitat atop the serra and on the slopes as far as the Rio Apiacas and a little beyond. We didn¿t continue past the headquarters of Fazenda Hiroshima where the forest has been cut over, but this road ostensibly leads to Juara. In May 2009 the road was in good condition from the MT-208 as far as the hydroelectric project, but appeared to deteriorate pretty quickly after Fazenda Hiroshima. That said, we encountered two pick-up trucks coming from Juara so it was probably passable at least in a 4-WD.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS835343133	2019-12-07 18:07:39	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			X				Ecuador	EC	Sucumbíos	EC-U							Sacha Lodge	L882540	H	-0.4710657	-76.4591897	2003-05-10		obsr146758	S62093610	Historical	P62	EBIRD				3	1		0	1	0		With local guide and an off duty Tropical Birding guide		
URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS184873807	2019-09-29 13:00:38	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			1				Ecuador	EC	Sucumbíos	EC-U							Sacha Lodge	L882540	H	-0.4710657	-76.4591897	2003-07-31	05:30:00	obsr103185	S13330350	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	840	4.828		6	1	G4545359	0	1	0		SACHA LODGE. Today started early with a predawn canoe trip across Pilchicocha Lake to Orquídea Creek trying to spotlight night birds. As usual Ferruginous Pygmy-Owls and Common Potoos were calling but we couldn't find any in the spotlight. We were somewhat successful with getting a distant Limpkin briefly in the light from Oscar's canoe. By daybreak we were slowly canoeing up the creek with a final destination of the kapok tree canopy tower. We would all be together in the kapok canopy tower. The tower was great and the birds came fast and furious. It was amazing to be in the tallest tree around and have birds landing all around. It is a whole other world in the top of a kapok tree with each limb the size of a normal tree. Priscilla, Breanna and I left the tower at 10:30a with David and Marcelo and birded slowly along the trail back to the dugout canoe where Bombo was waiting; then another leisurely trip back down the creek and to the lodge for lunch. After another mid-day swim in the lake we tried our hand at piranha fishing. A couple were caught; they are very small here. Priscilla and Breanna also tried their hand at swamping and un-swamping a dugout canoe with David. We then broke into our separate groups again. We spent the afternoon hours birding along the terra firme trails behind the lodge to metal tower #2 where darkness fell with us listening to a Tawny-bellied Screech-Owl. Again this is tough birding and few birds were seen but what we did see were new. We ran into our other group just after dark and tried with them to see a calling Long-tailed Potoo and Crested Owl but were unsuccessful. The highlight of the evening was when almost back to the lodge David sent Marcelo out into the darkness to see if he could find a known roost for Marbled Wood-Quail. He did and took David, Priscilla and me back to see these birds in the spotlight. We got back to the lodge at 7:20p, very tired, muddy and hungry but we made it to dinner only a little late. This was a long day and we were more than ready for cervezas and dinner back at the lodge!		
URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS90340308	2020-08-21 11:15:24	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			3				Ecuador	EC	Sucumbíos	EC-U							Sacha Lodge	L892333	P	-0.4002424	-76.6207123	2003-07-07	12:00:00	obsr107039	S6313862	Area	P23	EBIRD	1440		2.0234	3	1		0	1	0				
URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS178779205	2018-07-27 18:02:13	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			1				Ecuador	EC	Sucumbíos	EC-U							Sacha Lodge	L882540	H	-0.4710657	-76.4591897	2003-07-29	05:30:00	obsr103185	S12764936	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	750	8.047		6	1	G3367486	0	1	0		SACHA LODGE. Since our group was large (seven of us and five guides) we were divided into two groups. Priscilla, Breanna and I spent the morning, until 10:00a, on metal canopy tower #1 with our guide David Shackelford (23 years old from Houston, Texas), and two native Quichua guides Marcelo and Bombo; who I would come to know as some of the best birders I've ever been with. We had to hike through the terra firme forest in the dark to get there by sunup. Tom and Allison and Jim and Judy were in tower #2 with their guide Oscar Tupay and Carlos (son of Bombo), both Quichuas. By the end of the year these two towers are supposed to be connected with a rigid canopy walk. --Our first experience in an Amazon rainforest canopy tower was awesome. The morning started off quite foggy and we couldn't see tower 2, only 300 meters away, where Tom and Allison and Jim and Judy were. It lifted about an hour after getting to the tower. At 10:00a we came down from the tower and slowly birded our way back to the lodge along the Liana Grande Trail. We didn't see many birds on the hike back but what we did find was great. It takes a lot of work to see many of the terra firme birds, much time standing around playing tapes to get sometimes only a glimpse. We also observed leaf cutter ants, a strange insect that looked like a leaf and several beautiful butterflies and flowers. We got back to the lodge about 12:00p, had lunch at 1:00p and spent until 3:30p lounging around and swimming in Pilchicocha Lake which was very refreshing; and we didn't mind swimming with the piranhas, electric eels and sting rays! At 3:30p we got into the dugout canoe for a trip up Orquídea (Orchid Creek) Creek while the Mickels and Carlsons birded the Andén Walk. Orquídea Creek is Pilchicocha Lake's natural black water runoff to the Río Napo. In the dugout canoe we followed the winding stream through untamed palm forest to a landing near the base of the kapok tree observation tower and back.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS334599320	2019-12-04 11:56:02	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			1				Peru	PE	Madre de Dios	PE-MDD							Los Amigos Biological Station (CICRA)	L492606	H	-12.5662922	-70.1008415	2015-07-23	04:00:00	obsr110716	S24475056	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	1140	18.186		1	1		0	1	0		This was a big day at the end of my 2015 field season. Many birds were staked out using prior knowledge from 8 months of field work at Los Amigos. I walked a total of 18.15 km in 19 hours, so I averaged walking a little less than 1 km per hour. The skies were clear throughout the day; min/max temp 18/25ºC. This day was opportunistically selected since it was relatively cool from a friaje (winter storm) on the previous day. These cooler days make fantastic birding days for a number of reasons, including: 1) the birds are active throughout the day since there is no intense heat of the day, 2) relatively little insect noise throughout the day due to cooler temps, allowing for far better listening for bird song, and 3) clear skies allow for not only a decent raptor flight, but also slightly prolonged daylight around dusk and dawn. In addition, the moon was waxing half-full, so nocturnal birds were also relatively active. Habitats visited included: upper terrace forest, lower terrace forest, ridgeline forest, bamboo, semi-wet oxbow lake, oxbow lake, marsh, river/river-edge forest, palm swamp, and high overlooks for scanning canopy and open sky. Incidentally, I had two kinkajous, an olingo, a non-Giant armadillo sp., and a brocket deer sp. throughout the big day.----The general strategy was to visit various habitats, all of which were close and easily accessible from the station, and pick up various staked out birds along the way. I started the day on the upper terrace listening for targets in forest and bamboo, then the rest of the morning was spent on the lower terrace mostly around forest, lake and riverine habitat. In my experience, the activity of birds on the lower terrace is more dependent on the time of day than is activity on the upper terrace, so it made sense to knock out the lower terrace early on. In addition, I did not spend time picking through canopy flocks in the morning since these are still active in the afternoon. The afternoon was spent on the upper terrace targeting misses from the morning, upper terrace birds, canopy flocking species, and marsh birds at Cocha Raya.----Route:----(time: location. URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS639474553	2019-12-03 21:04:57	16668	species	Crowned Slaty Flycatcher	Empidonomus aurantioatrocristatus			1				Peru	PE	Madre de Dios	PE-MDD							Los Amigos Biological Station (CICRA)	L492606	H	-12.5662922	-70.1008415	2018-07-12	02:50:00	obsr336222	S47173526	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	1119	24.140		1	1		0	1	0		This was a Big Day during my 2018 field season at Los Amigos. I chose to do the Big Day the day after a three-day ‘friaje’ cold front had passed, following Sean Williams’ strategy regarding weather on his big day at this site in 2015. The weather for a short period of time after a friaje storm is typically cool with clear skies, conditions for excellent vocal activity throughout the day from birds that have kept quiet during the storm. This friaje passed slowly and the conditions were a little warmer and windier than I would have liked (min 16/max 28.5 C), but there was no intense heat and the conditions were still conducive to good vocal activity. The new moon cut down on night bird activity and a few normally easy species were difficult to find (in particular, large owls were very quiet).----The general layout of the route is detailed below. I focused on birding mature terra firme forest in the morning because this site has much more undisturbed, mature terra firme forest than equally mature forest in the floodplain, and in my experience the species diversity of mature terra firme at this site appears to meet, if not exceed, that of floodplain forest in the area. In addition to birds I saw a variety of monkey species, dwarf squirrel, and capybara.----Route:--(Time. Habitat. Comments.)----2:45-5:30 am: 1 to the top of the airstrip, then 10 to intersection with 8 and 24. Terra firme forest, landslide, early growth bamboo. Listening for various owls and potoos.----5:30-6:05 am: 8 to intersection with 20, stopping for ~10 min at the 8/23 intersection. Terra firme forest, listening for woodcreepers, furnariids, and other early morning singers.----6:05-8:30 am: 20 to 1 to 9 to Cocha Raya. Mature terra firme forest with ravines, and early growth bamboo on the air strip on 1. Picking up as many vocalizing birds as possible, including puffbirds, leaftossers, antbirds, and stakeouts like Black Bushbird and White-bearded Manakin.----8:30-9:15 am: Cocha Raya. Overgrown oxbow lake marsh, birding from along the edge along a cliff edge overlooking the lake. Many marsh and riparian growth species, like crakes, jacamars, hummingbirds, Little Cuckoo, and various other species. By this point had gotten a little warmer and windier.----9:15-11:15 am: 8 to 23 to 1 to the station. Hilly terra firme forest, secondary growth forest along 1, and a landslide along the Madre de Dios river. Activity generally low, but gradually picking up new species, including riverside species on the river at the landslide like swallows and Pied Lapwing.----11:15 am-12:15 pm: Around the station. Clearing with forest edge and a high bluff above the river to scan for raptors and other soaring birds. Not many raptors around, but located several species of austral migrant flycatchers.----12:15-1:25 pm: 10 to 28 to 19. Mixed bamboo and secondary growth forest. Targeting a few bamboo species I still needed, and several species that use the emergent trees above the low, dense bamboo, like Spangled Cotinga, Black-crowned Tityra, and Yellow-billed Nunbird.----1:25-4:30 pm: 15 to 30 to 18 to Cocha Amigos. Successional floodplain forest and scope views of a beach downriver on the Madre de Dios. Picking up easy floodplain species and working through a couple canopy flocks for tanagers, euphonias, and other species.----4:30-6:00 pm: Cocha Amigos, then 30 to 15 at dusk. Small oxbow lake for herons, flycatchers, Hoatzins, Wattled Jacanas, and various other oxbow lake specialties. At dusk, walked back along 15 to look for a few dusk-vocalizing species I had previously located during fieldwork with tinamous.----7:30-10:30: 1 to 20 to 2 to 1 and 10 in terra firme. Low activity, only added one new species - Black-banded Owl.	Flycatching from an emergent tree on 19.
